  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_e7258ee1-3563-42e6-b573-4acd07eca32f'

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1780738148" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16893314344827856822">This is a classic collection of stories in French about Nicolas and his inapt parents. Idyllic about life in the late 50s and early 60s, they are full of humour and tales of growing up. In France, they are like the equivalent of Tom Sawyer and Huck Finn.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer18302050381073449835"><b>Max And Lili Visit My School</b><br/><br/>Today when I arrived at school everyone was very excited because there were two new kids called Max and Lili. My friend Alceste told me they had come from the year 2012 in a time machine, I asked Alceste what a time machine was but he was eating a sandwich, Alceste eats all the time and his mouth is always full so he pointed at Agnan and told me to ask him.   <span id="freeText18302050381073449835" style="display:none"><b>Max And Lili Visit My School</b><br /><br />Today when I arrived at school everyone was very excited because there were two new kids called Max and Lili. My friend Alceste told me they had come from the year 2012 in a time machine, I asked Alceste what a time machine was but he was eating a sandwich, Alceste eats all the time and his mouth is always full so he pointed at Agnan and told me to ask him. Agnan is top of the class and the teacher's pet, he's no fun because he wears glasses so you can't hit him when you want to. He started to tell me what a time machine was but it was kind of boring so I went to look at the new kids.<br /><br />Max is cool, he's really good at soccer and he also likes fighting, I said he could join our gang and he said sure so now he's in my gang too. At break I went to talk to his sister, usually I don't talk to girls because they're dumb and just play with dolls and stuff but Lili looked a bit like my cousin Louisette who is cool so I thought why not. Lili told me all about life in 2012, it was really interesting, she got chased by a pedophile and her uncle got put in jail and her dad lost his job and she hangs out a lot on the Internet, I didn't know what the Internet was but Lili says it's like a TV with a typewriter and she met another pedophile there. Lili meets a lot of pedophiles, I asked her what they were and she told me, it's kind of gross but really interesting. After lunch, we had show and tell and teacher asked me to talk about something and I explained about pedophiles but teacher wasn't happy, she looked really tired and she told me to stand in the corner. I don't know why. <br /><br />Anyway it was Lili's fault because she explained it to me, maybe she didn't do it right and that's why teacher got mad. So at afternoon break I said she shouldn't tell me any more stuff and why didn't I tell her about life in 1960. Lili said fine and I said we fight a lot and we play soccer and I had just learned how to smoke. I had a cigar I got from my friend and I said would she like to try and she said yes please, so we went behind the bike shed and we tried smoking it. I coughed a lot and I felt a bit sick, but Lili was great and she could blow smoke out through her nose it was just like in the movies. <br /><br />We had almost finished smoking the cigar when Eudes came looking for us, Eudes is my friend he's a good kid and very strong and likes hitting everyone and he said Lili's mom was there with the time machine and they had to go back to 2012. So we came out and Lili's mom was talking to my mom, and they asked us if we had had fun and learned useful stuff, and I said I had learned what a pedophile was and Lili said she had learned to smoke, and my mom didn't look happy and Lili's mom didn't look happy either, and Lili's mom said they had to go right now and my mom said that was a good idea.<br /><br />I hope Lili comes back tomorrow, she is almost as cool as Louisette, if Louisette doesn't want to marry me when I grow up then I will marry Lili instead.<br /></span>

<div id="review_205623177" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/205623177" />
    <a title="Emily" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/343944-emily"><img alt="Emily" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1242156693p2/343944.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/205623177?book_show_action=true">Sep 05, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily" href="/user/show/343944-emily">Emily</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780714845296" href="/book/show/128654.Nicholas">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/343944-emily?shelf=read-aloud">read-aloud</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/343944-emily?shelf=read-for-school">read-for-school</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer205623177" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3411141759295512102">I have fond memories of reading some of these stories in their original form (I think) in my 10th grade French class (sadly, these are the ONLY fond memories I have of studying French!). Goscinny's endearingly naughty little boys made a wonderfully refreshing change from the forced profundities of Le Petit Prince, to say nothing of the banal social lives of the dopey looking Parisian teens who populated a text-book called "Nos Amis." Sempe's cartoonishly simply but wickedly expressive illustrati</span>
  <span id="freeText3411141759295512102" style="display:none">I have fond memories of reading some of these stories in their original form (I think) in my 10th grade French class (sadly, these are the ONLY fond memories I have of studying French!). Goscinny's endearingly naughty little boys made a wonderfully refreshing change from the forced profundities of Le Petit Prince, to say nothing of the banal social lives of the dopey looking Parisian teens who populated a text-book called "Nos Amis." Sempe's cartoonishly simply but wickedly expressive illustrations also added a great deal of charm. So I always thought I'd like to go back and revisit Nicholas, perhaps even in French, but this relatively recent and highly attractively produced English-language edition made it easy and pleasant to be lazy. Truth be told, this time around, I might have found the stories to be more rewarding if I had had to work harder when reading them. As it was, I found them amusing, but they get a little repetitive. Most of the book I read aloud to my eight-year-old, who giggled a lot, but also asked me to stop reading sometimes, and skip to the next chapter, because he gets a little anxious when things go wrong in stories -- and these particular stories are not so subtle that he couldn't see that such things as playing hooky and smoking a purloined cigar were not going to end well. In fact, sometimes I felt distinctly uneasy myself wondering what my son made of all the of cheerful punches to the nose in this book, and the regret at not being able to whack the teacher's pet because of his glasses. Also Goscinny does so much winking over Nicholas' head at the adult reader, who is clearly meant to sympathize with the overwhelmed teachers and parents, that one almost wonders if it's meant for children at all. So, to put it more succinctly, I enjoyed it, but am slightly relieved it's over.<br /><br />Next time, or one of the sequels perhaps, en français? Well, no harm in being optimistic!</span>
  <a data-text-id="3411141759295512102" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer557575775" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16160437377575542431">Reading Le Petit Nicolas series was a great way to improve my fluency in French. It was easy enough to read for pleasure and the vocabulary repeated enough so I actually learned new words! I used these words in conversation with my French teachers and friends while I lived in France and they were quite impressed because I was using slang. Since this book is written for kids, it helped me learn the language like they did. The sentences were quite easy to translate and I got into the rhythm of the</span>
  <span id="freeText16160437377575542431" style="display:none">Reading Le Petit Nicolas series was a great way to improve my fluency in French. It was easy enough to read for pleasure and the vocabulary repeated enough so I actually learned new words! I used these words in conversation with my French teachers and friends while I lived in France and they were quite impressed because I was using slang. Since this book is written for kids, it helped me learn the language like they did. The sentences were quite easy to translate and I got into the rhythm of the language. I also read passages from the book aloud to help me with my accent and speaking. <br /><br />I loved this little fellow. He is a good guy who gets into trouble rather often, so most of us can relate to him. </span>
  <a data-text-id="16160437377575542431" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/4119240?book_show_action=true">Aug 05, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kimberlee" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kimberlee" href="/user/show/196697-kimberlee">Kimberlee</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780714844824" href="/book/show/1018218.Nicholas">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Ages 8-ish and up</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer4119240" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16986035993275699031">I read this book to review for the library I work at, and I seriously just pulled it off the shelf because I liked the way the cover looked. It's about a young French boy, Nicholas, and his school friends. It's written in first-person as Nicholas, and what I found particularly endearing was the way the sentences read as though they were really written by a seven year old. They run on, but are clear to understand. Each chapter is like a short story or an individual episode, and his reactions to t</span>
  <span id="freeText16986035993275699031" style="display:none">I read this book to review for the library I work at, and I seriously just pulled it off the shelf because I liked the way the cover looked. It's about a young French boy, Nicholas, and his school friends. It's written in first-person as Nicholas, and what I found particularly endearing was the way the sentences read as though they were really written by a seven year old. They run on, but are clear to understand. Each chapter is like a short story or an individual episode, and his reactions to the things that happen are very unique. Example "...Alec hit him on the cap with his tomahawk and said he was taking him prisoner and Rufus was upset because he'd dropped his whistle in the grass and I was crying a bit and telling Eddie this was my yard and I never wanted anything to do with him again, and everyone was shouting and it was all great, we were having a fantastic time." Adults will probably appreciate the quaintness of this book better than children, but it's a fun read for anyone, and a quick, easy read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16986035993275699031" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer7423814539121855805">What a hysterical book! This is a French translation that was originally published in 1959, so it depicts a time that has gone by (Nicholas points out that his family doesn't have a television yet). But both kids and adults will enjoy this first person account of incidents in Nicholas' life. We see how much fun young boys have just being boys. For instance, Nicholas describes playing cowboys with his friends. When no one will volunteer to be tied up to be the prisoner, his dad volunteers. This p</span>
  <span id="freeText7423814539121855805" style="display:none">What a hysterical book! This is a French translation that was originally published in 1959, so it depicts a time that has gone by (Nicholas points out that his family doesn't have a television yet). But both kids and adults will enjoy this first person account of incidents in Nicholas' life. We see how much fun young boys have just being boys. For instance, Nicholas describes playing cowboys with his friends. When no one will volunteer to be tied up to be the prisoner, his dad volunteers. This prompts the next door neighbor to come over to taunt his dad and the boys have a great time watching all of this until they are called in for dinner. "I never knew Dad liked playing cowboys so much. When we came down later in the evening Mr. Billings had been gone a long time, but there was Dad still tied to the tree, shouting and making faces. Fancy being able to play games all by yourself! My dad is great!"</span>
  <a data-text-id="7423814539121855805" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1246328295" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1246328295" />
    <a title="Kara" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10864046-kara"><img alt="Kara" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1357568280p2/10864046.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1246328295?book_show_action=true">Apr 05, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kara" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kara" href="/user/show/10864046-kara">Kara</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1246328295" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15838621996716492194">The book contains a series of 16 short stories, by the end of which you get to know all the little guys and the weird adults (well, according to Nicholas). The stories lend snapshots into the seemingly simple life of an 8-year-old boy shuffling between home and school. All the adults end up feeling horrified at some point, be it the parents, the teacher or just a random seller in a toy store. The kids never stop making us scream, sigh and fall sick. The best part is that they do it unintentional</span>
  <span id="freeText15838621996716492194" style="display:none">The book contains a series of 16 short stories, by the end of which you get to know all the little guys and the weird adults (well, according to Nicholas). The stories lend snapshots into the seemingly simple life of an 8-year-old boy shuffling between home and school. All the adults end up feeling horrified at some point, be it the parents, the teacher or just a random seller in a toy store. The kids never stop making us scream, sigh and fall sick. The best part is that they do it unintentionally and conclude that the adults are such a bore for not liking the good weather (cause who wants to deal with a bunch of kids bickering on the playground on a fine day) . Elegantly chaotic, I would say. On second thoughts, not so elegant since I don't think I have picked up so many fighting words and name callings in such a short reading. I'm so glad I attempted reading this in French, finishing it and feeling 400 words richer.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15838621996716492194" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_177034278" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/177034278" />
    <a title="Jill" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2523448-jill"><img alt="Jill" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1404710143p2/2523448.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/177034278?book_show_action=true">Jun 15, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jill" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jill" href="/user/show/2523448-jill">Jill</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780714845296" href="/book/show/128654.Nicholas">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer177034278" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17157916968641430491">I judged a book by its spine and chose this book off the shelf at the library!<br/><br/>This is a book originally written in French which has been translated into English. It's told in the point-of-view of a little boy, probably about seven years old. He gets into a ton of funny situations and he is always in trouble and fighting with his friends.<br/><br/>This is like the French version of Junie B. Jones, in that both of the books have a very authentic kid voice! This book was funny, and it really sounded like a s</span>
  <span id="freeText17157916968641430491" style="display:none">I judged a book by its spine and chose this book off the shelf at the library!<br /><br />This is a book originally written in French which has been translated into English. It's told in the point-of-view of a little boy, probably about seven years old. He gets into a ton of funny situations and he is always in trouble and fighting with his friends.<br /><br />This is like the French version of Junie B. Jones, in that both of the books have a very authentic kid voice! This book was funny, and it really sounded like a seven-year-old was telling the story. I felt bad for the poor teacher - she taught 30 crazy boys!!! Geez louise.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_2477711997" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2477711997" />
    <a title="Kelley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/29588908-kelley"><img alt="Kelley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1548895841p2/29588908.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2477711997?book_show_action=true">Aug 17, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kelley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kelley" href="/user/show/29588908-kelley">Kelley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780714861159" href="/book/show/9712321-nicholas">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2477711997" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12360283002467072642">Right about the time Beverly Cleary was bringing Ramona to life, Goscinny and Sempe were introducing the French world to Nicholas. In the last decade or so, English readers have finally gotten the chance to meet him.<br/><br/>In some dreamworld where the two children could cross paths, they would find in each other sweet commiseration for the miseries of childhood inflicted by adults who just don’t understand.<br/><br/>Nicholas faithfully reports everything just as he sees it in his world of school, home and the em</span>
  <span id="freeText12360283002467072642" style="display:none">Right about the time Beverly Cleary was bringing Ramona to life, Goscinny and Sempe were introducing the French world to Nicholas. In the last decade or so, English readers have finally gotten the chance to meet him.<br /><br />In some dreamworld where the two children could cross paths, they would find in each other sweet commiseration for the miseries of childhood inflicted by adults who just don’t understand.<br /><br />Nicholas faithfully reports everything just as he sees it in his world of school, home and the empty lot. Like most young children, he is an absolutist and a literalist.<br /><br />The day of a school inspection, the teacher warns against speaking or laughing out of turn. The inspector opens his presentation with a joke.<br /><br />“It’s a pity our teacher had told us not to laugh without permission, because we could hardly restrain ourselves. … The inspector laughed a lot, but then he didn’t need anyone’s permission. However, when he saw that the whole class was quite quiet he put his eyebrows back into place and coughed …” <br /><br />Nicholas won’t let you lose track of his gang. The key members are reintroduced the first time they appear in every chapter.<br /><br />“Alec is my friend who is very fat and who eats all the time, perhaps I may have mentioned him before,” he says three pages from the end of the book. Yes, he had.<br /><br />“Cuthbert is top of the class and teacher’s pet and we aren’t all that mad about him only we can’t hit him much because of his glasses.”<br /><br />When the teacher leaves the room once and asks Cuthbert to keep an eye on things, Cuthbert instructs the other boys to work on a math problem. <br /><br />“So Matthew asked if he was out of his tiny mind,” Nicholas reports. <br /><br />Teachers, parents and principals are traumatized by the fights and pranks and name-calling. Nicholas is always confused by that. <br /><br />In one ball game, someone’s crying, someone just got kicked in the shins, and someone else’s new shirt is torn. “Eddie, who’d been waiting patiently in his own goal, got fed up and started punching the noses closest to him, which happened to belong to his own side. We were all shouting and running around and we were having a really fabulous time!”<br /><br />You really should join the fun.<br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12360283002467072642" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2686004039" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2686004039" />
    <a title="Heidi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/803808-heidi"><img alt="Heidi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1358206962p2/803808.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2686004039?book_show_action=true">Apr 27, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Heidi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Heidi" href="/user/show/803808-heidi">Heidi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2686004039" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5791142656646978204">I picked this out as a classic beginning French book to read/translate with my daughter while we have been living in Paris. It was obviously a little outdated because it was written in the 50s -- Nicholas and his friends are always insulting each other and beating each other up on the playground. Probably is a better book for a 12-year-old boy, but we got a good laugh from the funny scuffles and mischievous antics!</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3452420925" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3452420925" />
    <a title="Jo Coleman" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/39966417-jo-coleman"><img alt="Jo Coleman" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1423568844p2/39966417.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3452420925?book_show_action=true">Jul 20, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jo Coleman" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jo Coleman" href="/user/show/39966417-jo-coleman">Jo Coleman</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3452420925" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4701772409516854686">Good fun, with excellent plotting of the chaos that can ensue whenever small boys get together and do... pretty much anything. The illustrations are awesome, though unfortunately sometimes they spoilt the punchline of the story by appearing a couple of pages too early. Just about easy enough for me to slog through several dozen years after French A-level, and I learned some key vocabulary about punching people on the nose.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1963234833" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Alexandria" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/26959944-alexandria"><img alt="Alexandria" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582145960p2/26959944.jpg" /></a>

<div id="review_2960838936" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2960838936" />
    <a title="Ginny Kestel" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/64658280-ginny-kestel"><img alt="Ginny Kestel" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1604041434p2/64658280.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2960838936?book_show_action=true">Oct 08, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ginny Kestel" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ginny Kestel" href="/user/show/64658280-ginny-kestel">Ginny Kestel</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2960838936" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17074873843761769148">This was the first book I read in a completely different language: French. It is written for children, but when you’re reading in a language that isn’t your mother tongue, you have to start with something that you can understand without the overwhelming length of a novel with too many words and phrases that ruin the reading experience. The illustrations by Goscinny are a lovely accompaniment to the stories. The book itself is comprised of several chapters that account different stories from the </span>
  <span id="freeText17074873843761769148" style="display:none">This was the first book I read in a completely different language: French. It is written for children, but when you’re reading in a language that isn’t your mother tongue, you have to start with something that you can understand without the overwhelming length of a novel with too many words and phrases that ruin the reading experience. The illustrations by Goscinny are a lovely accompaniment to the stories. The book itself is comprised of several chapters that account different stories from the perspective of the main character Nicolas. The stories were very funny. Reading this in French was extremely helpful in learning new vocabulary and seeing how much I remembered from my high school French classes. I understood about 70% of the text, but of course, I had a French to English dictionary nearby in case I needed to look a word up. One of my new favorite words is “le chouchou” or “the teacher’s pet,” describing the character Agnan. Such a delightful read. If you’re learning French or want to brush up on your skills, I absolutely recommend this.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17074873843761769148" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_986011159" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/986011159" />
    <a title="Ed Cottingham" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32788767-ed-cottingham"><img alt="Ed Cottingham" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/986011159?book_show_action=true">Jul 04, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ed Cottingham" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ed Cottingham" href="/user/show/32788767-ed-cottingham">Ed Cottingham</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer986011159" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer769473000288509026">It would be hard to overstate the charm of these wonderful stories. Like many others, I picked up this book to help with my project of trying to teach myself French. Not only does it serve that purpose, but it is so engaging that it has held me on course when the inherent difficulty of the language and some cross-cultural exasperation has tempted me to chuck the whole project. No way could I ever write this little dude and his copains out of my life.<br/><br/>Although hilarious, the Nicolas stories also t</span>
  <span id="freeText769473000288509026" style="display:none">It would be hard to overstate the charm of these wonderful stories. Like many others, I picked up this book to help with my project of trying to teach myself French. Not only does it serve that purpose, but it is so engaging that it has held me on course when the inherent difficulty of the language and some cross-cultural exasperation has tempted me to chuck the whole project. No way could I ever write this little dude and his copains out of my life.<br /><br />Although hilarious, the Nicolas stories also touch you in a much deeper place. He is a little boy full of life and good humor, but he and his friends are also filled with every possible anxiety about growing up and finding their manly places in the world. They are charmingly obsessed with their status and their dignity.<br /><br />One of my favorite stories is "Louisette," which recounts the visit of a young girl who comes with her mother for tea. Nicolas is pouty from the beginning as his mother dresses him up, in his view, like a clown. And maman assures him that if he doesn't show that he is well raised, he will have an affair with her!<br /><br />Although Nicolas is always filled with explanations that burst forth in run-on sentences, this traumatic visit brings him close to tears more than once. In Nicolas's world, not crying is one of the main imperatives. Another is assuming a male's naturally dominant [irony] and superior role over young girls, who, after all, cry all the time.<br /><br />Louisette starts off telling Nicolas that he looks like a monkey and things go downhill from there. She is so much more quick-witted, not to mention athletic, that she repeatedly leaps ahead and distracts him just when he is deciding whether to give her a punch in the nose or to pull her hair. And it is Louisette who is landing all the successful coups on Nicolas. Meanwhile, Louisette is always batting her eyelashes at the mamans and impressing them with what an adorable innocent she is!<br /><br />As with the "Louisette" story of a young boy having to deal with a very formidable young girl who does not fit into his template defining his superior place in the world, all these stories are filled with very real anxieties of male childhood. Let me say again, though, they are very, very funny! You love this kid.<br /><br />How easy/difficult is this book for a student of French. There are definitely difficult bits such as when Nicolas is playing cowboys and describes all the various cowboy accoutrements that he and his friends have hung on themselves. Often, too, sentences are very run-on, mimicking Nicolas's overflowing emotions and self-justifications. And the mannerisms of his speech are realistic and more difficult than the dry dialogue of textbooks. But this is worth a little difficulty - I just want to caution against expecting a child's book to be extremely easy. It is manageable, but not in the first few weeks of studying French.<br /><br />I also have a two-CD set of these stories read in French. The CD set is a dramatic reading and it is an absolute delight. But it is considerably more difficult than the book. Those run-on sentences are read in rapid bursts, as intended. The reading wonderfully captures the charm of the book but definitely does not make it any easier.<br /><br />My only exasperation with the Nicolas books is that I cannot share them with my English-only friends. They touched me so much and made me laugh so hard. I hope I have inspired someone here. (Originally posted on Amazon in 2006.)</span>
  <a data-text-id="769473000288509026" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_478623216" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/478623216" />
    <a title="Cruth" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12723605-cruth"><img alt="Cruth" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1392864210p2/12723605.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/478623216?book_show_action=true">Dec 15, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cruth" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cruth" href="/user/show/12723605-cruth">Cruth</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780714845296" href="/book/show/128654.Nicholas">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12723605-cruth?shelf=read-aloud">read-aloud</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12723605-cruth?shelf=childrens-chapter-book">childrens-chapter-book</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer478623216" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer260551410934281885">Nicholas - written by Rene Goscinny, (who wrote Asterix) and illustrated by Jean-Jacques Sempe.<br/><br/>Originally published in France, 1959, as "Le petit Nicolas", this edition was first published in 2005 (my version from 2007). Translated by Anthea Bell.<br/><br/>I should admit outright I was never much of a fan of Asterix. I never really got the humour. Maybe 'cause I'm a girl - my brothers all liked them. And so perhaps some of the story here is not my thing because it is so male-centric.<br/><br/>Each chapter stands as</span>
  <span id="freeText260551410934281885" style="display:none">Nicholas - written by Rene Goscinny, (who wrote Asterix) and illustrated by Jean-Jacques Sempe.<br /><br />Originally published in France, 1959, as "Le petit Nicolas", this edition was first published in 2005 (my version from 2007). Translated by Anthea Bell.<br /><br />I should admit outright I was never much of a fan of Asterix. I never really got the humour. Maybe 'cause I'm a girl - my brothers all liked them. And so perhaps some of the story here is not my thing because it is so male-centric.<br /><br />Each chapter stands as a self contained story of around 6 pages (book has 127 pages, and 19 chapters).<br /><br />As a read aloud, it struggles. Told from a little boy's pov (Nicholas) and in his voice, we have many run on sentences. The frequency of them makes the story harder to follow. And more difficult for an early reader to read.<br /><br />Nicholas attends a boys school, and his friends are all boys. No female characters, and we have stereotypically male child scenarios. The boys physically fight, disobey the teacher, argue, call each other names (bullying/teasing). It is treated as normal behaviour and they do not have consequences. As a book from which children model behaviour - it isn't my cup of tea. In every story someone gets told off and cries, someone else is punched on the nose, and they are all having a really good time. I just don't get it.<br /><br />But the 6yo enjoys it. And the teen, who loved this book 7 years ago, is enjoying listening in. They like the slapstick-ish child humour, they read/hear the "naughty boy" scenarios and think "boy, wouldn't that be fun? but we so would get in trouble" or "boys are like that", and keep going. They see more in this book than I do.<br /><br />Illustrations are infrequent - we get a large illustrative drawing as we begin the chapter, small ones in the next pages. More text than drawing. But the images are lovely and whimsical. Definitely add to the book.<br /><br />The language itself uses a simple, easy vocabulary. No particularly difficult words. However, children would be confronted with "walls of text", which is often very off-putting. The ability of the child to concentrate on reading an entire page of text has to be learnt and practiced - you couldn't expect a too new reader to comfortably tackle "Nicholas".<br /><br />Overall, I liked it. It was an unusual, interesting read that appealed to the kids.<br /><br />Age (taking into account comprehension, concentration, language):<br />Read aloud - 6+<br />Read yourself - 9+</span>
  <a data-text-id="260551410934281885" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('xY6h8Q0MlCmVb1y1ZpPjrM1cpDRpvYxnDxPqtIk+UisJ/2ffIpKIGkGfxUWjw6/lDlXHH/DG4+etEHY61HIT0A==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('M/yLzaCL6XYhAtxjvrceum1bO/ZTItyRXB9Ea/3RYfj/jU3jjxX1RfXyRZN751LzrlJY3cpZsxH+HNjloJ0gAw==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer16002089710352029589">René Goscinny (1926 - 1977) was a French author, editor and humorist, who is best known for the comic book <i>
  <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/series/41270-asterix' rel='nofollow noopener'>Asterix</a>
</i>, which he created with illustrator <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/26082.Albert_Uderzo' title='Albert Uderzo' rel='nofollow noopener'>Albert Uderzo</a>, and for his work on the comic series <i>Lucky Luke</i> with Morris (considered the series' golden age).</span>
  <span id="freeText16002089710352029589" style="display:none">René Goscinny (1926 - 1977) was a French author, editor and humorist, who is best known for the comic book <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/41270-asterix" rel="nofollow noopener">Asterix</a>
</i>, which he created with illustrator <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/26082.Albert_Uderzo" title="Albert Uderzo" rel="nofollow noopener">Albert Uderzo</a>, and for his work on the comic series <i>Lucky Luke</i> with Morris (considered the series' golden age).</span>
